Orbital parameters were about 200 × 225 miles (321 × 366 kilometers).\n\n## Landing\nNASA's NEAR Shoemaker spacecraft landed on the surface of the 21-mile long asteroid Eros on February 12, 2001. The spacecraft was undamaged and operational after the landing at an estimated speed of 1.5 to 1.8 meters per second (thus becoming the first spacecraft to soft-land on an asteroid).\n\n## Instruments\nNEAR Shoemaker was a three-axis stabilized spacecraft that carried a six-instrument scientific payload: a multispectral imager (MSI), a near-infrared spectrometer (NIS), a laser rangefinder (NLR), an X-ray spectrometer (XRS), a γ-ray spectrometer (GRS), and a magnetometer (MAG). The total mass of the instruments was 56 kg (123 lb), requiring 80 watts of power.\n\n## Cost\nThe mission was flown under NASA's Discovery program, a series of low-cost (less than about $150 million in mid-1990s dollar amounts) planetary science projects.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"974a5faf-f4b7-4aa0-b483-016ee4f12459","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:29:22.914Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"5ac89ba4-4317-4e43-bbd2-73e635684231","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"main","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Mars Global Surveyor became the first successful mission to the red planet in two decades.\n\n## Orbital Parameters\n\nAfter a 10-month journey, Mars Global Surveyor took up a highly elliptical orbit above Mars on September 12, 1997. It employed a technique known as aerobraking to achieve a final 400-km circular polar orbit in which it circled Mars 12 times a day. After aerobraking ended in February 1999, MGS was in a 118 minute circular polar science mapping orbit with an index altitude of 378 km. The orbit is sun-synchronous (2 a.m./2 p.m.).\n\n## Scientific Instruments\n\nThe Mars Orbiter Camera (MOC) used 3 instruments: a narrow angle camera that took high resolution images and red and blue wide angle cameras for context and daily global imaging. Additional instruments included:\n\n- The Mars Orbiter Laser Altimeter (MOLA) was designed to determine Mars's global topography.\n- The Thermal Emission Spectrometer (TES) mapped the mineral composition of the surface by scanning thermal emissions.\n- A magnetometer and electron reflectometer (MAG/ER) determined that Mars does not have a global magnetic field but rather many smaller localized fields.\n- The Ultrastable Oscillator (USO/RS) used precise clock measurements to map variations in the gravitational field.\n\n## Mission Cost\n\nThe Mars Global Surveyor mission cost about $154 million to develop and build and $65 million to launch. Mission operations and data analysis cost approximately $20 million/year.\n\n## Major Discoveries\n\nMajor findings included dramatic evidence that water still flows on Mars in short bursts down hillside gullies, and the identification of water-related mineral deposits leading to selection of a Mars rover landing site for a subsequent mission. In its first three years of operation, Mars Global Surveyor returned more data about Mars than all prior Mars missions combined.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"cdbcaabf-b03f-4bf3-a287-ecf0e027c3df","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:29:39.784Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"7637eb3d-1759-42f4-a5a8-e3d1c075f489","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"main","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

NASA\",\"url\":\"https://www.nasa.gov/history/25-years-ago-mars-pathfinder-launches-to-mars-to-deploy-sojourner-the-first-planetary-rover/\"},{\"title\":\"Mars Pathfinder - NASA Science\",\"url\":\"https://science.nasa.gov/mission/mars-pathfinder/\"},{\"title\":\"Mars Sojourner Rover Model | National Air and Space Museum\",\"url\":\"https://airandspace.si.edu/collection-objects/mars-pathfinder-mini-rover-full-scale-model/nasm_A20020297000\"},{\"title\":\"Mars Pathfinder, the start of modern Mars… | The Planetary Society\",\"url\":\"https://www.planetary.org/space-missions/pathfinder\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here's comprehensive information about Mars Pathfinder and the Sojourner rover:\n\n## Launch Date\nMars Pathfinder was launched on December 4, 1996, by NASA aboard a Delta II booster, and landed on July 4, 1997, on Mars's Ares Vallis.\n\n## Landing Site\nThe landing site was located at 19.30° north latitude and 33.52° west longitude in Ares Vallis, which is called Chryse Planitia, a part of the Oxia Palus quadrangle.\n\n## Instruments\nBoth the lander and the 23-pound (10.6 kilogram) rover, Sojourner, carried instruments for scientific observations. Included were scientific instruments to analyze the Martian atmosphere, climate, geology, and the composition of its rocks and soil. Specifically, the six-wheeled Sojourner carried two black-and-white cameras used for navigating the surface, one colour camera, and an alpha proton X-ray spectrometer for determining the composition of rocks and soil.\n\n## Mass\nThe spacecraft consisted of a lander and a lightweight, 10.6 kg (23 lb) wheeled robotic Mars rover named Sojourner.\n\n## Cost\nWhile the flagship Viking missions cost a whopping $7 billion (inflation-adjusted for 2020), Pathfinder was relatively low-cost at $485 million.\n\n## Discoveries\nMars Pathfinder returned 2.3 billion bits of information, including more than 16,500 images from the lander and 550 images from the rover, as well as more than 15 chemical analyses of rocks and soil and extensive data on winds and other weather factors. Findings from the investigations carried out by scientific instruments on both the lander and the rover suggest that Mars was at one time in its past warm and wet.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"9e15ca19-c244-4e20-95ee-cbd0ed9f073a","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:29:50.950Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"4e35ccb7-44c2-4489-98e7-a4dec6e0b8e2","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

The launch vehicle was a Titan-IVB/Centaur at Cape Canaveral, United States.\n\n## Mass and Dimensions\nCassini-Huygens weighed 5.6 tonnes and measured 6.7 m high by more than 4 m wide. The Cassini orbiter weighed 2,125 kg (4,685 pounds) and was 6.7 metres (22 feet) long and 4 metres (13 feet) wide. The Huygens probe weighed 349 kg (769 pounds), was 2.7 metres (8.9 feet) across, and carried six instruments designed to study the atmosphere and surface of Titan.\n\n## Cost\nThe cost of the mission was $3.9 billion.\n\n## Instruments\nCassini's 12 scientific instruments included imaging cameras, radar, spectrometers and magnetometers: the Imaging Science Subsystem (ISS), Cassini radar (RADAR), Radio Science Subsystem (RSS), Ion and Neutral Mass Spectrometer (INMS), Visible and Infrared Mapping Spectrometer (VIMS), Composite Infrared Spectrometer (CIRS), Cosmic Dust Analyser (CDA), Radio and Plasma Wave Spectrometer (RPWS), Cassini Plasma Spectrometer (CAPS), Ultraviolet Imaging Spectrograph (UVIS), Magnetospheric Imaging Instrument (MIMI) and Dual-technique Magnetometer (MAG).\n\nThe Huygens probe comprised six instrument packages: the Huygens Atmosphere Structure Instrument (HASI), Gas Chromatograph and Mass Spectrometer (GCMS), Aerosol Collector and Pyrolyser (ACP), Descent Imager/Spectral Radiometer (DISR), Doppler Wind Experiment (DWE) and the Surface Science Package (SSP).\n\n## Saturn, Titan, and Enceladus\nCassini-Huygens entered Saturn orbit on July 1, 2004. Huygens was released on December 25, 2004, and landed on Titan on January 14, 2005—the first landing on any celestial body beyond Mars.\n\nKey discoveries included: During the first two close flybys of the moon Enceladus in 2005, Cassini discovered a deflection in the local magnetic field characteristic of a thin but significant atmosphere, with ionized water vapor as its main constituent. Cassini also observed water ice geysers erupting from the south pole of Enceladus.\n\n## Grand Finale\nThe Grand Finale consisted of the spacecraft being directed into Saturn from April 2017 to September 15, 2017. After 23 \"proximal\" orbits, a final encounter with Titan changed Cassini's orbit so that on September 15, 2017, it ended its mission by plunging into Saturn, which allowed Cassini to sample Saturn's atmosphere directly and avoid any possible future contamination of Enceladus and Titan.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"d4e8cb66-51e6-4670-af12-92902dd01415","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:30:18.285Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"cda182bc-bd32-4e47-a62b-a7c4f92f7c59","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Additionally, a Doppler gravity experiment would globally scour the lunar surface.\n\n## Key Discoveries - Water Ice at Poles\nIn March 1998, NASA announced that data from Lunar Prospector suggested the presence of water ice at both the lunar poles. The neutron spectrometer instrument detected hydrogen, assumed to be in the form of water. Its ion propulsion engine had operated for 16,265 hours, far longer than any previous spacecraft, and provided a total velocity change of three miles per second, the largest achieved by any spacecraft with its own propulsion system.\n\n## Encounters with Asteroid Braille and Comet Borrelly\n\nOn July 29, 1999, it flew past asteroid Braille. Although the probe was pointed in the wrong direction and did not obtain the high-resolution images scientists wanted, the mission was an overall success.\n\nOn September 22, 2001, it successfully navigated its way past Comet Borrelly, providing excellent views of the ice particles, dust, and gas leaving comets. The spacecraft came within 2,200 km (1,400 miles) of the roughly 8 × 4-km (5 × 2.5-mile) cometary nucleus.\n\n## Instruments\n\nThe mission included various scientific instruments. The spacecraft was able to use all four of its instruments at Borrelly, which included black-and-white pictures, infrared spectrometer measurements, ion and electron data, and measurements of the magnetic field and plasma waves around the comet.\n\n## Mission Cost\n\nThe search results did not contain specific information about the mission cost.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"efbe4d2a-144b-4dc5-9029-ba36b5efd958","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:30:40.763Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"f2ae3c1d-dee5-46f7-8f0d-233c83154cf1","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Mars Missions - NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory | NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory (JPL)\",\"url\":\"https://www.jpl.nasa.gov/missions/mars-climate-orbiter/\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here is comprehensive information about the Mars Climate Orbiter failure:\n\n## Mission Details\n\nThe Mars Climate Orbiter was built at a cost of $125 million and was a 638-kilogram robotic space probe launched by NASA on December 11, 1998. It was designed to study the Martian climate, Martian atmosphere, and surface changes and to act as the communications relay in the Mars Surveyor '98 program for Mars Polar Lander.\n\n## The Units Error\n\nThe root cause for the loss of the MCO spacecraft was the failure to use metric units in the coding of a ground software file, \"Small Forces,\" used in trajectory models. More specifically, the software calculated the force that the thrusters needed to exert in pounds of force, and a second piece of code that read this data assumed it was in the metric unit—\"newtons per square meter\".\n\nDuring the design phase, the propulsion engineers at Lockheed Martin in Colorado expressed force in pounds, while the navigation team at the Jet Propulsion Laboratory (JPL) used the metric system of millimeters and meters in its calculations.\n\n## Failure Details\n\nThe increased AMD (Angular Momentum Desaturation) events coupled with the fact that the angular momentum (impulse) data was in English, rather than metric, units, resulted in small errors being introduced in the trajectory estimate over the course of the 9-month journey, resulting in the spacecraft trajectory being approximately 170 kilometers lower than planned.\n\nIn September of 1999, after almost 10 months of travel to Mars, the Mars Climate Orbiter burned and broke into pieces. Last contact with the spacecraft was on Sept. 23, 1999, nine months after launch, and an investigation found that the spacecraft burned up in Mars' atmosphere.\n\n## Instruments and Technical Specifications\n\nThe spacecraft weighed 638 kg (1,407 lb) and included eight hydrazine monopropellant thrusters: four 22 N (4.9 lbf) thrusters to perform trajectory corrections and four 0.9 N (3.2 ozf) thrusters to control attitude. The spacecraft also included a LEROS 1B main engine rocket, providing 640 N (140 lbf) of thrust.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"0a4f01ab-d904-4093-8c0d-608dd0517792","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:31:06.916Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"2c96a9a2-027d-4173-9a83-a3e750116295","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

The total cost of the Mars Polar Lander was US$165 million, with spacecraft development costing US$110 million, launch estimated at US$45 million, and mission operations at US$10 million.\n\n## Mass and Spacecraft Details\n\nThe Mars Polar Lander was a 290-kilogram uncrewed spacecraft lander designed to study the soil and climate of Planum Australe, a region near the south pole on Mars.\n\n## Instruments\n\nThe spacecraft would employ a robotic arm to dig into the layered terrain of Mars' unexplored polar landscape and deploy a pair of microphones for soil-moisture experiments. The lander also carried two Deep Space 2 Mars Microprobes, penetrators which would separate and bury themselves into the Martian surface 100 km away from the main landing point.\n\n## Cause of Loss\n\nOn December 3, 1999, at 14:39:00 UTC, the last telemetry from Mars Polar Lander was sent, just prior to cruise stage separation and the subsequent atmospheric entry, and no further signals were received from the spacecraft. \n\nThe Failure Review Board concluded that the most likely cause of the mishap was a software error that incorrectly identified vibrations, caused by the deployment of the stowed legs, as surface touchdown. The resulting action by the spacecraft was the shutdown of the descent engines, while still likely 40 meters above the surface. Inadequate funding and poor management have been cited as underlying causes of the failures.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"b0ec1b5d-1b91-4388-b959-0727f3cb868c","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:31:21.970Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"38c24005-a3cc-4dcd-9b5c-72df11b6c3f7","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

On Jan. 15, 2006, Stardust's Sample Return Capsule (SRC) separated from the main vehicle and four hours later, it entered Earth's atmosphere.\n\nNote: The search results did not contain specific information about the mission's total cost.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"5bae0a27-3f25-4bb7-8f8e-7b0d7bbbd6f7","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:31:34.402Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"6ce9102c-0bd0-480a-b7b8-463989a0b280","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Under the command of Col. Eileen Collins, the shuttle lifted off the launch pad at John F. Kennedy Space Center in Cape Canaveral, Florida.\n\n## Mass and Payload\n\nThe Chandra X-ray Observatory was the heaviest payload ever carried by the Space Shuttle system, at 22,780 kilograms (50,222 lb).\n\n## Mission Crew\n\nThe STS-93 crew included Commander Eileen M. Collins, the first woman to command a space shuttle mission, Pilot Jeffrey S. Ashby, and Mission Specialists Catherine \"Cady\" G. Coleman, Steven A. Hawley, and Michel A. Tognini of the French Space Agency (CNES).\n\n## Deployment and Instruments\n\nChandra was deployed by Cady Coleman from Columbia at 11:47 UTC. At its launch, Chandra was the most sophisticated X-ray observatory ever built.\n\n## Orbital Parameters\n\nIn its final orbit, the distance of Chandra from Earth ranged from 16,000 km (9,942 miles) to 133,000 km (about 82,646 miles), more than a third of the way to the moon. The orbit is a Highly Elliptical Orbit with a perigee of ~10,000 km and an apogee of ~140,000 km, inclination = 76.72°, period of ~64 hours.\n\n## Mission Accomplishments\n\nWith a planned five-year lifetime, Chandra continues its observations after a quarter century. The identifier \"AM-1\" refers to its orbit, passing over the equator in the morning.\n\n## Instruments\n\nTerra features five onboard instruments, each with varying imaging capabilities for specific functions; ASTER, CERES, MISR, MODIS and MOPITT. The US provided the spacecraft, the launch, and three instruments developed by NASA (CERES, MISR, MODIS). Japan provided ASTER and Canada MOPITT.\n\n## Mass and Cost\n\nWeight: 5,190 kg (11,442 lbs.) at launch. Regarding cost, Cost: $1.3 billion, including spacecraft, U.S. instruments and launch vehicle (does not include ground system cost nor the cost of the Canadian or Japanese instruments.\n\n## Earth Observing System\n\nIt is the flagship of the Earth Observing System (EOS) and the first satellite of the system which was followed by Aqua (launched in 2002) and Aura (launched in 2004).\n\n## Scientific Discoveries and Achievements\n\nTerra's five sensors help us understand out changing planet and provide critical data used in applications from food security, volcanic monitoring, wildfire safety, public health, and climate modeling. \"Terra was the quintessential and most significant of all of the EOS satellites that made contributions to all aspects of Earth science,\" and \"All five of the Terra [instruments] made significant and, in many cases, first-of-a-kind global observations relevant to climate change.\"\n\nNo other Earth science mission has been as productive as Terra; its exponential increase in data distribution has driven many changes in science data systems.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"1d8fabbb-d0d0-4189-a868-53069d94640a","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:32:03.913Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"0f534e1f-7c2f-4495-9201-53cf4d79c844","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

More specifically:\n\n- Energetic neutral atom imagers (LENA, MENA, HENA) used hydrogen, helium, and oxygen atoms in the exosphere to form images and determine the properties of their low-, medium- and high-energy parent ions\n- Ultraviolet imagers (FUV and EUV), where the extreme ultraviolet (EUV) imager detects light from helium atoms in Earth's plasmasphere, and the Far ultraviolet (FUV) imager employs three detectors to image the auroras in different wavelengths and measure the distribution of different ions\n\n## Major Discoveries\nThe spacecraft produced a wealth of images of the previously invisible region of space in the inner magnetosphere and exceeded all its scientific goals.\n\n## Loss of Contact\nAlmost six years later, it unexpectedly ceased operations in December 2005 during its extended mission and was declared lost. Specifically, contact was lost on Dec. 18, 2005.\n\n## Recovery\nThe IMAGE spacecraft was re-discovered in January 2018 after more than twelve years of silence. Amateur astronomer Scott Tilley in Roberts Creek, British Columbia, using his home satellite detection rig, detected the signal on January 20, 2018.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"cc9a66ef-c176-407e-9d34-ad57b6e43f2d","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:32:17.858Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"0aaf1d35-cd05-4bb7-9ef0-c2104190b9a1","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

After 33 orbits of the Earth, and a series of rendezvous maneuvers performed by Gidzenko, they docked the Soyuz capsule to the aft port of the Zvezda Service Module on 2 November 2000, at 09:21 UTC.\n\n## Major Activities\n\nDuring their mission, the Expedition 1 crew activated various systems on board the station, unpacked equipment that had been delivered, and hosted three visiting Space Shuttle crews and two uncrewed Russian Progress resupply vehicles. Although much of their four-month mission was spent getting the space station ready for many future crews to live (somewhat) comfortably, they also performed the first scientific experiment on the ISS.\n\n## Historical Significance\n\nIt was the beginning of an uninterrupted human presence on the station which continues as of 2026.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"8eec694f-e97a-49e6-b221-4a4ac14afaf0","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:32:29.450Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"696dd2a3-e1e5-4605-80bc-88c084949cb4","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

It combines a 5-wavelength visual imaging system with a 9-wavelength infrared imaging system.\n\n## Spacecraft Mass and Cost\nThe spacecraft has a launch mass of 725.0 kg, including 348.7 kg of fuel. The project was developed by NASA, and contracted out to Lockheed Martin, with an expected cost for the entire mission of US$297 million.\n\n## Orbital Parameters\nAs of October 2019 it is in a polar orbit around Mars with a semi-major axis of about 3,800 km or 2,400 miles. The spacecraft is in a 2-hour orbit around Mars.\n\n## Major Discoveries\nOn May 28, 2002 (sol 210), NASA reported that Odyssey's GRS instrument had detected large amounts of hydrogen, a sign that there must be ice lying within a meter of the planet's surface, and proceeded to map the distribution of water below the shallow surface. Both the collector arrays and the concentrator contain suites of ultra-high purity target materials, each tailored to enable the analysis of a different element family. Additionally, the spacecraft carried ion and electron monitors to measure solar wind properties.\n\n## Mass\nThe spacecraft had a mass of 494 kilograms (1,089 pounds).\n\n## Cost\nThe mission's cost, including development, mission operations, and sample analysis, was approximately $209 million.\n\n## Crash Landing and Recovery\nThe sample return capsule crash-landed in Utah on September 8, 2004, after a design flaw prevented the deployment of its drogue parachute. The SRC impacted into the desert of Utah causing some damage. Despite the crash, the recovered science canister arrived at Johnson Space Center in Houston on October 4, 2004. Although most collectors were damaged, some were successfully recovered, and the Genesis science team demonstrated that some contamination could be removed or avoided, and that the solar wind particles could be analyzed using a variety of approaches, achieving all of the mission's major science objectives.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"ecf94ed9-2b49-4e21-b5f3-ea483f98fa9c","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:32:54.857Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"600c315c-cfb2-4f46-a03c-f311eed0879a","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Opportunity operated for almost 15 years, and it was operational on Mars for 5111 sols (14 years, 138 days on Earth).\n\n## Key Instruments\nA suite of instruments (MB, APXS, the magnets, MI, and RAT) were deployed on a robotic arm (known as the Instrument Deployment Device, IDD).\n\n## Major Discoveries\nOpportunity found evidence that Mars may once have been able to sustain microbial life. Key discoveries included finding meteorites and exploring multiple craters. Mission highlights included the initial 90-sol mission, finding meteorites such as Heat Shield Rock (Meridiani Planum meteorite), and over two years of exploring and studying Victoria crater.\n\nDue to the planetary 2018 dust storm on Mars, Opportunity ceased communications on June 10 and entered hibernation on June 12, 2018.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"c6614e50-adbf-4091-a94c-8e6dae85f47e","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:33:48.270Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b1f1ab51-a7df-470f-bce5-d34ae0035c15","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

The total mission cost was $1.36 billion.\n\n## Mass and Instruments\n\nThe Spitzer Space Telescope had a launch mass of 950 kg. The satellite contained three instruments that allowed it to perform astronomical imaging and photometry from 3.6 to 160 micrometers, spectroscopy from 5.2 to 38 micrometers, and spectrophotometry from 55 to 95 micrometers.\n\n## Orbital Parameters\n\nSpitzer was placed into a heliocentric orbit trailing and drifting away from Earth's orbit at approximately 0.1 astronomical units per year (an \"Earth-trailing\" orbit).\n\n## Infrared Capabilities\n\nThe primary mirror is 85 centimeters (33 in) in diameter, f/12, made of beryllium and was cooled to 5.5 K (−268 °C; −450 °F).\n\n## Mission Duration and End\n\nThe Spitzer Space Telescope was an infrared space telescope that was active between 2003 and 2020. The planned mission period was 2.5 years, with liquid helium exhaustion expected to occur after five or slightly more years, which occurred on 15 May 2009. On Jan. 30, 2020, engineers decommissioned the spacecraft, bringing the Spitzer mission to a close.\n\n## Key Discoveries\n\nSpitzer revealed a wispy ring of Saturn, the most remote galaxy ever detected, and the first known star system with seven Earth-sized exoplanets — Trappist-1.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"877e85a0-1d3c-44fc-8416-dbbc5aad4789","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:34:00.522Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"edaa7f37-58d0-4ffb-a6ea-d75288eabcea","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Here are the key findings:\n\n## The Foam Strike and Immediate Cause\n\n82 seconds after launch a large piece of foam insulating material, the \"left bipod foam ramp\", broke free from the external tank and struck the leading edge of the shuttle's left wing, damaging the protective carbon heat shielding panels. More specifically, at 81.7 seconds after launch, when the Shuttle was at about 20,000m and traveling at Mach 2.46, a large piece of insulating foam came off the External Tank left bipod ramp area, and the foam impacted under the leading edge of the left wing at 81.9 seconds.\n\n## CAIB Findings\n\nThe CAIB investigation confirmed the immediate cause of the accident as a foam strike to the leading edge of the shuttle's left wing during launch and criticized NASA for bad organizational and safety culture. The panel determined that the accident was caused by foam insulation breaking off from the external fuel tank, forming debris which damaged the orbiter's wing, and that the problem of \"debris shedding\" was well known but considered \"acceptable\" by management.\n\n## The Crew\n\nThe seven-member crew — Rick Husband, commander; Michael Anderson, payload commander; David Brown, mission specialist; Kalpana Chawla, mission specialist; Laurel Clark, mission specialist; William McCool, pilot; and Ilan Ramon, payload specialist from the Israeli Space Agency were all killed during reentry.\n\n## Mission Details\n\nThe flight launched from Kennedy Space Center in Florida on January 16, 2003. It spent 15 days, 22 hours, 20 minutes, 32 seconds in orbit. The disaster occurred during reentry while the orbiter was over Texas.\n\n## Investigation Results\n\nThe CAIB released its final report on August 26, 2003.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"0f6bf49c-46ab-48b2-8bce-df3f1007e3cc","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:34:12.508Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"2d9bb095-4aa9-4dfd-a0e1-d5b71df09cd6","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

The Energetic Particle and Plasma Spectrometer (EPPS) was mounted on the side and top deck and the magnetometer (MAG) was at the end of the 3.6 m boom.\n\n## Mass\nThe 10-foot-wide (3 meters) spacecraft was the spacecraft's dimension, though specific mass information wasn't detailed in the search results.\n\n## Cost\nThe $450 million MESSENGER spacecraft launched on Aug. 3, 2004.\n\n## Orbital Insertion\nMESSENGER finally entered orbit around Mercury at 00:45 UT March 18, 2011, nearly seven years after launch.\n\n## End of Mission\nDuring a final six-week extension, onboard propellant was finally exhausted, and because no further orbit-correction maneuvers were possible the spacecraft crashed onto Mercury's surface on April 30, 2015.\n\n## Key Discoveries\nDuring its stay in Mercury orbit, the probe's instruments yielded significant data, including a characterization of Mercury's magnetic field and the discovery of water ice at the planet's north pole. Among the major findings were that Mercury harbors water ice and organic compounds at its north pole, that volcanism played a major role in shaping the planet's surface, and that Mercury's surface materials are more volatile-rich and chemically reduced than expected.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"26a793d3-a3fd-48fd-8c09-25d5d22ba2ec","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:34:24.554Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"a0ba0aee-ef74-4d95-975d-3ad81d9b29e8","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

{"parentUuid":"e3f707cd-b8d9-457b-9de2-c1c2d85e5bf2","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"ea4b4095-6634-4f61-a4ea-252488a65bc6","agentId":"a9f8c27073cb69431","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01NYmPsbn8wU8W4q5QmQt5f4","type":"tool_result","content":"Web search results for query: \"Deep Impact EPOXI mission comet Tempel 1 impactor 2005 launch date instruments mass cost discoveries\"\n\nLinks: [{\"title\":\"Deep Impact (EPOXI) - NASA Science\",\"url\":\"https://science.nasa.gov/mission/deep-impact-epoxi/\"},{\"title\":\"Deep Impact (spacecraft) - Wikipedia\",\"url\":\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_Impact_(spacecraft)\"},{\"title\":\"Deep Impact | Comet Exploration & NASA Mission | Britannica\",\"url\":\"https://www.britannica.com/topic/Deep-Impact-space-probe\"},{\"title\":\"Deep Impact / EPOXI (Discovery 7)\",\"url\":\"https://space.skyrocket.de/doc_sdat/deep_impact.htm\"},{\"title\":\"Deep Impact - Asteroid & Comet Missions - NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory | NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory (JPL)\",\"url\":\"https://www.jpl.nasa.gov/missions/deep-impact/\"},{\"title\":\"Deep Impact: A Comet-Hunting Mission | Space\",\"url\":\"https://www.space.com/43236-deep-impact.html\"},{\"title\":\"NASA's Deep Impact Produced Deep Results | NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory (JPL)\",\"url\":\"https://www.jpl.nasa.gov/news/nasas-deep-impact-produced-deep-results/\"},{\"title\":\"NASA Slammed a Probe Into a Comet 10 Years Ago Today | Space\",\"url\":\"https://www.space.com/29848-nasa-deep-impact-comet-collision-anniversary.html\"},{\"title\":\"Deep Impact\",\"url\":\"http://www.astronautix.com/d/deepimpact.html\"},{\"title\":\"SBN Mission Support: Deep Impact\",\"url\":\"https://pdssbn.astro.umd.edu/data_sb/missions/deepimpact/index.shtml\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here's comprehensive information about the Deep Impact EPOXI mission:\n\n## Launch Date and Mission Overview\n\nDeep Impact was a NASA space probe launched from Cape Canaveral Air Force Station on January 12, 2005. The spacecraft delivered a special impactor into the path of Tempel 1 to reveal never-before-seen materials and provide clues about the internal composition and structure of a comet.\n\n## Impactor Specifications\n\nThe impactor weighed 820 pounds (372 kilograms) and was traveling at a relative velocity of about 23,000 miles per hour (37,000 kilometers per hour) at the time of impact. The impact generated an explosion the equivalent of 4.7 tons of TNT and a crater estimated to be about 490 feet (150 meters) in diameter.\n\n## Mission Cost\n\nThe $330 million Deep Impact mission launched in January 2005. Additionally, the total cost of the extended mission is $40 million.\n\n## Instruments\n\nThe flyby spacecraft carried two primary instruments, high- and medium-resolution imagers, with the radio system used as a third experiment to measure possible velocity changes due to the comet's mass or atmospheric drag. The imagers had filters to highlight diatomic carbon and cyanogen molecules in the debris. An infrared spectrometer was designed to detect water, carbon monoxide, and carbon dioxide.\n\n## Key Discoveries\n\nTempel 1 has a very fluffy structure made up of a fine dust that is weaker than a bank of powder snow, but that's held together by gravity; what appear to be impact craters can be seen on the surface of the comet; a huge increase of carbon-containing materials were detected when analyzing the comet's ejection plume, indicating that comets contain a substantial amount of organic material and may have brought that material to Earth at one time; and the comet's interior is well shielded from solar heating, meaning that the ice and other material deep within the comet nucleus may be unchanged from the early days of the solar system.\n\n## Extended Mission (EPOXI)\n\nBecause the flyby vehicle still had plenty of propellant, on July 3, 2007, NASA approved a new supplemental mission for Deep Impact, known as EPOXI. The name was derived from the combination of the two components of this extended flight: Extrasolar Planet Observations (EPOCh) and Deep Impact Extended Investigation (DIXI).\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"79844da3-5c11-4907-a458-d630710fce4a","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:34:39.822Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e3f707cd-b8d9-457b-9de2-c1c2d85e5bf2","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

It consists of a 0.5 m (19.7 in) aperture reflecting telescope, the largest so far of any deep space mission, which allows it to take pictures of Mars with resolutions of 0.3 m/pixel.\n\n## Spacecraft Mass and Other Instruments\n\nMRO has a mass of approximately 2180 kg. The spacecraft is equipped with a visible stereo imaging camera (HiRISE) with resolution much better than one meter and a visible/near-infrared spectrometer (CRISM) to study the surface composition, along with an infrared radiometer, an accelerometer, and a shallow subsurface sounding radar (SHARAD) to search for underground water.\n\n## Data Returned\n\nAs of July 29, 2023, the MRO has returned over 450 terabits of data. The MRO takes around 29,000 images per year.\n\n## Key Discoveries\n\nHiRISE has imaged Mars exploration rovers on the surface, including the Opportunity rover and the ongoing Curiosity mission. The Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter has sent back thousands of stunning images of the Martian surface that are helping scientists learn more about Mars, including the history of water flows on or near the planet's surface.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"9af3c41d-ba8f-437e-8be2-dec2e7eff228","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:34:55.272Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"05f3bc51-e658-4497-8583-a912e930f087","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

The spacecraft launched with a speed of about 16.26 km/s (10.10 mi/s; 58,500 km/h; 36,400 mph), which still holds the record for fastest launch speed from Earth.\n\n## Spacecraft Specifications\n\nThe 465 kg launch mass includes 80 kg of propellant, and the spacecraft has a mass of 385 kg. The New Horizons science payload consists of seven instruments — three optical instruments, two plasma instruments, a dust sensor and a radio science receiver/radiometer.\n\nKey instruments include:\n- The Long Range Reconnaissance Imager (LORRI), a telescopic camera built to enable distant imaging of the farthest regions of the solar system\n- Ralph, the main \"eyes\" of New Horizons and is charged with making the maps that show what Pluto, its moons, and other Kuiper Belt Objects look like\n- The Alice ultraviolet imaging spectrometer, the PEPSSI plasma-sensor, and the LORRI long-range visible-spectrum camera\n\n## Mission Cost\n\nTotal cost for New Horizons over the entire 15 year mission, was $700 million, including spacecraft and instrument development, launch vehicle, mission operations, data analysis, and education/public outreach.\n\n## Pluto Flyby\n\nIt was launched in 2006, becoming the first spacecraft to perform a flyby study of the Pluto system in 2015. At closest approach, the spacecraft came about 7,750 miles (12,500 kilometers) from Pluto and about 17,900 miles (28,800 kilometers) from its largest moon, Charon.\n\n## Arrokoth (Ultima Thule) Flyby\n\nA secondary mission contained a flyby and study of one or more other Kuiper belt objects (KBOs) in the decade to follow, where it flew past 486958 Arrokoth in 2019.\n\n### Speed and Distance at Arrokoth\n\nThe spacecraft flew by the object at a speed of 51,500 km/h (32,000 mph; 14.3 km/s) and within 3,500 km (2,200 mi). Arrokoth was a Kuiper Belt Object that is approximately 4 billion miles (6.4 billion kilometers) from Earth.\n\n### Arrokoth Discoveries\n\n**Shape and Composition:**\nArrokoth is a contact binary—a \"snowman\"-shaped object composed of two lobes connected by a narrow neck of material. The lobes of Arrokoth, named Wenu and Weeyo, are believed to be former planetesimals that once formed a binary system, but gently merged together.\n\nEnd to end, the overall shape of Arrokoth measures about 22 miles (35 kilometers) long. It's about 12 miles (20 kilometers) wide, by 6 miles (10 kilometers) thick.\n\n**Key Scientific Findings:**\nEverything about Arrokoth — including its color, shape and composition — suggests it was born via cloud collapse rather than accretion. It's also very red – even redder than Pluto. The estimated bulk density of (486958) Arrokoth, approximately 235 kg/m³, is among the lowest for explored small bodies in the outer Solar System, indicating a highly porous interior dominated by void space rather than compact material.\n\n**Naming:**\nBefore the flyby on 1 January 2019, NASA invited suggestions from the public on a nickname to be used for the object. One of the choices, Ultima Thule, was selected on 13 March 2018. In November 2019, the International Astronomical Union (IAU) announced the object's permanent official name, Arrokoth. Arrokoth means \"sky\" in the Powhatan/Algonquian language.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"2d6bcf0c-dc50-4785-996c-954732ba1ca8","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:35:19.163Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"6690915d-c2d5-4ae3-9848-be68e0ac575f","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

NEAR Shoemaker: Technical Details Extract\n\n## Launch Information\n- **Date/Time**: February 17, 1996, 20:43:27 UTC\n- **Vehicle**: Delta II 7925-8 (with nine solid-rocket boosters and Star 48 third stage)\n- **Site**: Cape Canaveral Air Force Station Space Launch Complex 17B\n\n## Spacecraft Specifications\n- **Launch Mass**: 805 kg\n- **Dry Mass**: 487 kg (1,074 lb)\n- **Power Output**: 1,800 watts at 1 AU\n- **Shape**: Octagonal prism, approximately 1.7 m per side\n- **Antenna**: Fixed 1.5 m X-band high-gain radio antenna\n\n## Mission Timeline\n- **Mathilde Flyby**: June 27, 1997 (1,212 km closest approach)\n- **Orbital Insertion at Eros**: February 14, 2000\n- **Landing**: February 12, 2001 (~20:01 UTC)\n- **Last Contact**: February 28, 2001\n- **Total Duration**: 5 years, 21 days\n\n## Eros Orbit Parameters\n- Initial: 321 × 366 km elliptical orbit\n- Final achieved: 35 km circular polar retrograde orbit\n- **Total Orbits**: 230 completed\n\n## Scientific Instruments (56 kg total mass, 80W power)\n1. **Multi-Spectral Imager (MSI)**: Visible surface imaging\n2. **NEAR IR Spectrograph (NIS)**: 0.8–2.6 micrometer spectral range in 62 bins\n3. **Magnetometer**: DC to 10 Hz measurement capability\n4. **X-ray/Gamma-Ray Spectrometer (XGRS)**: Two-part system (X-ray fluorescence and gamma-ray detection with BGO shield)\n5. **Laser Rangefinder (NLR)**: Direct-detection single-pulse capability\n\n## Mission Cost\n\"The final total mission cost was $224 million, which consisted of $124.9 million for spacecraft development, $44.6 million for launch support and Here are the key results:\n\n### Plume Composition\n\nNearly 98 percent of the gas in the plume is water vapor, about 1 percent is hydrogen, and the rest is a mixture of other molecules including carbon dioxide, methane and ammonia. Additionally, the plume contains traces of methane, ammonia, carbon monoxide, carbon dioxide and various salts and simple organic molecules.\n\n### Molecular Hydrogen & Hydrothermal Processes\n\nThe Ion Neutral Mass Spectrometer onboard the Cassini spacecraft detected molecular hydrogen in the plume. The most plausible source of this hydrogen is ongoing hydrothermal reactions of rock containing reduced minerals and organic materials. This drives the ocean out of chemical equilibrium, in a similar way to water around Earth's hydrothermal vents, potentially providing a source of chemical energy.\n\n### Organic Molecules\n\nRecent research has expanded on organic findings. Unprecedented high encounter speeds revealed previously unobserved molecular fragments, allowing the identification of aliphatic, (hetero)cyclic ester/alkenes, ethers/ethyl and, tentatively, N- and O-bearing compounds. Ice grains contained concentrated, complex, macromolecular organic material with molecular masses above 200u.\n\n### Implications\n\nEnceladus' ocean floor could include features analogous to hydrothermal vents on Earth, which are known to support life on the seafloor.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"57cc550c-6605-4207-8afa-df1836e76e06","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:36:41.008Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"6121e38b-19c8-4585-9520-b40c6a16fc37","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Wikipedia\",\"url\":\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens\"},{\"title\":\"ESA Science & Technology - Cassini grand finale\",\"url\":\"https://sci.esa.int/web/cassini-huygens/-/59048-cassini-grand-finale\"},{\"title\":\"ESA Science & Technology - Grand finale orbits\",\"url\":\"https://sci.esa.int/web/cassini-huygens/-/59047-grand-finale-orbits\"},{\"title\":\"ESA - Grand finale orbits\",\"url\":\"https://www.esa.int/ESA_Multimedia/Images/2017/04/Grand_finale_orbits\"},{\"title\":\"Cassini's Grand Finale - NASA Science\",\"url\":\"https://science.nasa.gov/resource/cassinis-grand-finale/\"},{\"title\":\"Saturn Surprises As Cassini Continues its Grand Finale | NASA Jet Propulsion Laboratory (JPL)\",\"url\":\"https://www.jpl.nasa.gov/news/saturn-surprises-as-cassini-continues-its-grand-finale/\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here are the details about Cassini's Grand Finale:\n\n## Timeline and Orbits\n\nIn April 2017, Cassini was placed on an impact course that unfolded over five months of daring dives—a series of 22 orbits that each passed between the planet and its rings. More specifically, a final close flyby of the moon Titan on April 22 used the moon's gravity to reshape Cassini's trajectory so that the spacecraft leapt over the planet's icy rings to pass between the rings and Saturn. The spacecraft began its finale on April 26 and will continue its dives until Sept. 15, when it will make a mission-ending plunge into Saturn's atmosphere.\n\n## The Gap Between Saturn and Its Rings\n\nEvery week, Cassini dived through the approximately 1,200-mile-wide (2,000-kilometer-wide) gap between Saturn and its rings. No other spacecraft had ever explored this unique region. During 22 such passes over about five months, the spacecraft's altitude above Saturn's clouds varied from about 1,000 to 2,500 miles (1,600 to 4,000 kilometers), thanks to occasional distant passes by Titan that shifted the closest approach distance.\n\n## Final Plunge\n\nOn Sept. 15, 2017, the spacecraft made its final approach to the giant planet Saturn. Cassini dived into the planet's atmosphere, sending science data for as long as its small thrusters could keep the spacecraft's antenna pointed at Earth. Soon after, Cassini burned up and disintegrated like a meteor.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"2d6fd93c-8546-42b6-a06a-60cda0ac97a5","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:36:52.990Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e5b8bf12-e2cb-43f0-a4b3-f52d58e78ba5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

More specifically, the spacecraft dry mass is 10,560 pounds (4,790 kg).\n\n## Key Instruments\n\nThe Chandra X-ray Observatory is equipped with four main science instruments:\n\n**ACIS (Advanced CCD Imaging Spectrometer):** ACIS consists of 10 CCD chips and provides images as well as spectral information of the object observed. It operates in the photon energy range of 0.2–10 keV.\n\n**HRC (High Resolution Camera):** The HRC has two micro-channel plate components and images over the range of 0.1–10 keV. It also has a time resolution of 16 microseconds.\n\n**Transmission Gratings:** The High Energy Transmission Grating Spectrometer (HETGS) works over 0.4–10 keV and has a spectral resolution of 60–1000. The Low Energy Transmission Grating Spectrometer (LETGS) has a range of 0.09–3 keV and a resolution of 40–2000.\n\n## Major Discoveries\n\nChandra has made numerous groundbreaking discoveries. The first light image, of supernova remnant Cassiopeia A, gave astronomers their first glimpse of the compact object at the center of the remnant, probably a neutron star or black hole. Additional discoveries include:\n\n- Chandra showed for the first time the shadow of a small galaxy as it is being cannibalized by a larger one, in an image of Perseus A\n- A new type of black hole was discovered in galaxy M82, mid-mass objects purported to be the missing link between stellar-sized black holes and super massive black holes\n- Sound waves from violent activity around a super massive black hole were observed in the Perseus Cluster (2003)\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"b18ace14-5af7-4774-aa25-a873cf7428d1","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:37:06.183Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"01f4e572-9b58-4604-a8ab-6ea15b7790ea","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Mercury Dual Imaging System (MDIS)**\n- Narrow-angle and wide-angle CCD cameras on pivoting platform\n- Full surface map at 250 m/pixel resolution\n- Regional imaging at 20–50 m/pixel\n- Color imaging via narrow-band filter wheel\n\n**2. Gamma-Ray Spectrometer (GRS)**\n\"Measured gamma-ray emissions from the surface of Mercury to determine the planet's composition\"\n- Depth penetration: 10 cm\n- Detected: O, Si, S, Fe, H, K, Th, U\n\n**3. Neutron Spectrometer (NS)**\n- Hydrogen detection to 40 cm depth via cosmic ray collisions\n- Mapped abundance across northern hemisphere\n- Investigated water ice in shaded craters\n\n**4. X-Ray Spectrometer (XRS)**\n- Mapped mineral composition within top millimeter\n- Elements: Mg, Al, S, Ca, Ti, Fe\n- Energy range: 1–10 keV\n\n**5. Magnetometer (MAG)**\n- Detailed magnetic field measurements\n- Characterized magnetospheric interactions\n\n**6. Mercury Laser Altimeter (MLA)**\n- Topographic mapping via infrared laser reflection (1,064 nm wavelength)\n- High-precision northern hemisphere mapping\n- Surface reflectivity measurements\n\n**7. Mercury Atmospheric and Surface Composition Spectrometer (MASCS)**\n- Exosphere characterization via ultraviolet emissions\n- Iron and titanium detection via infrared reflectance\n\n**8. Energetic Particle and Plasma Spectrometer (EPPS)**\n- Magnetosphere charged particles (EPS component)\n- Surface-originated ions (FIPS component)\n\n**9. Radio Science (RS)**\n- Gravity field measurements\n- Planetary core investigation via positioning data\n- Libration amplitude quantification\n\n## Gravity Assists\n**Earth Flyby:** August 2, 2005 (2,347 km altitude)\n**Venus Flyby 1:** October 24, 2006 (2,990 km altitude)\n**Venus Flyby 2:** June 5, 2007 (337 km altitude)\n**Mercury Flyby 1:** January 14, 2008 (200 km altitude)\n**Mercury Flyby 2:** October 6, 2008 (200 km altitude)\n**Mercury Flyby 3:** September 29, 2009 (228 km altitude)\n\n## Key Discoveries\n\n**Magnetic Field:** Field offset \"far to the north of the planet's center\"\n\n**Water Ice & Organics:** \"Discovery of water ice at the planet's north pole\" in permanently shadowed craters, plus \"carbon-containing organic compounds\"\n\n**Volcanism:** \"Visual evidence of past volcanic activity on the surface of Mercury\"\n\n**Exosphere:** \"Large amounts of water present in Mercury's exosphere\"; unexpectedly high Mg and Ca concentrations\n\n**Core:** \"Evidence for a liquid iron planetary core\"\n\n**Tectonics:** Detection of previously unknown fault scarps indicating \"Mercury is still contracting\"\n\n**Surface Composition:** Most detailed and accurate 3D maps to date; gravity anomalies mapping subsurface structure\n\n**Additional Achievement:** First observation of lunar eclipse from another planet (October 8, 2014)\n\n## Impact Specifics\n**Impact Velocity:** 14,080 km/h (8,750 mph)\n**Estimated Crater Diameter:** ~16 m (52 ft)\n**Detection:** Confirmed via loss of Deep Space Network signal at 19:40 GMT"}]},"uuid":"7e642dc7-25a1-4ce6-b5a3-caa09f42e59d","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:38:56.246Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"809ab0e4-bfe1-4cb7-8d4f-99e3a509180e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

eight far-infrared channels\n\n**MARCI (Mars Color Imager):**\n- Five visible and two ultraviolet bands\n- \"Collects about 84 images\" daily\n- 1-10 km pixel resolution\n\n**SHARAD (Shallow Radar):**\n- HF radio waves: 15-25 MHz range\n- Layer resolution: 7 meters minimum\n- Maximum depth: 3 km penetration\n\n## Data & Discoveries\n\n**Data Returned:** \"Over 450 terabits of data\" as of July 29, 2023\n**Images:** \"Takes around 29,000 images per year\"\n\n**Key Discoveries:**\n\n1. **Water Ice:** \"New craters on Mars have excavated relatively pure water ice\" that sublimates after exposure\n\n2. **Mineral Deposits:** Identified \"chloride minerals\" and \"nine to ten different classes of minerals formed in the presence of water\" including phyllosilicates, carbonates, and sulfates\n\n3. **Recurring Slope Lineae:** \"Dark streaks on slopes...caused by what appeared to be flowing salty water on the surface or subsurface of Mars,\" though \"further research suggested that the dark streaks were created by grains of sand and dust slipping down slopes\"\n\n4. **Landing Site Support:** Helped select safe landing sites for Phoenix (2008), Curiosity (2012), InSight (2018), and Perseverance (2021)\n\n## Current Status\nAs of January 2024, the spacecraft \"has around 132 kg of fuel remaining, enough to support operations until 2035,\" and is on its sixth extended mission phase."}]},"uuid":"e9bdd10e-2d00-4b29-b892-e87d2cff23bc","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:39:45.495Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b4934052-669b-4bb0-b57f-a91233309983","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Here's a summary of the key facts:\n\n## Deep Space 1 Mission Overview\n\n**Mission Cost:**\nDeep Space 1 has a total mission cost of $152.3 million comprised of $94.8 million for development, $43.5 million for launch, $10.3 million for operations, and $3.7 million for science.\n\n**Spacecraft Mass:**\nThe spacecraft's gross mass was 486 kg (1,072 lb).\n\n**Propellant Details:**\nThe launch mass of the spacecraft included 31.1 kg of hydrazine and 81.5 kg of xenon gas. The fuel consisted of 31 kg (68 lb) of hydrazine for attitude control thrusters and 82 kg (181 lb) of xenon for the NSTAR ion engine.\n\n**NSTAR Ion Engine:**\nThe NASA Solar Technology Application Readiness (NSTAR) electrostatic ion thruster, developed at NASA Glenn, achieves a specific impulse of 1000–3000 seconds. The NSTAR/IPS system consists of a 30 cm xenon ion thruster, xenon feed system (XFS), Power Processing Unit (PPU), and a Digital Control and Interface Unit (DCIU). Although the engine produces just 92 millinewtons (0.33 ozf) thrust at maximal power (2,100 W on DS1), the craft achieved high speeds because ion engines thrust continuously for long periods.\n\n**Mission Success:**\nAll 12 technology tests were successful, and the mission is credited with proving the effectiveness of ion engines for long-duration spaceflight and advancing the field of spacecraft navigation.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"e872abf4-9af2-4a09-9875-f5fb194eb68d","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:40:37.827Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"9d284c35-9766-4d28-9ae6-1898367d536a","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

The Pressure Modulated Infrared Radiometer (PMIRR) uses narrow-band radiometric channels and two pressure modulation cells to measure atmospheric and surface emissions in the thermal infrared and a visible channel to measure dust particles and condensates.\n\n## Mission Objectives\n\nThe mission would observe and study dust storms, weather systems, clouds and dust hazes, ozone, distribution and transport of dust and water, the effects of topography on atmospheric circulation, atmospheric response to solar heating, and surface features, wind streaks, erosion, and color changes. The orbiter would also serve as a data relay satellite for the Mars Polar Lander and other future NASA and international lander missions to Mars.\n\n## Cost\n\nThe Mars Surveyor '98 program spacecraft development cost 193.1 million dollars, with launch costs estimated at 91.7 million dollars and mission operations at 42.8 million dollars. CONTOUR's four scientific instruments were designed to take detailed pictures and measure the chemical makeup of each comet's nucleus while analyzing the surrounding gas and dust.\n\n## Objectives\nThe Comet Nucleus Tour (CONTOUR) Discovery class mission had as its primary objective close fly-bys of two comet nuclei with the possibility of a fly-by of a third known comet or an as-yet-undiscovered comet. Scientific objectives included imaging the nuclei at resolutions of 4 m, performing spectral mapping of the nuclei at resolutions of 100-200 m, and obtaining detailed compositional data on gas and dust in the near-nucleus environment, with the goal of improving our knowledge of the characteristics of comet nuclei.\n\n## Target Comets\nThe flight plan called for CONTOUR to streak past the comet 2P/Encke on Nov. 12, 2003, passing within 62 miles or so of its icy nucleus. Here's a comprehensive summary of the key instruments found on both Spirit and Opportunity:\n\n## MER Instrument Overview\n\nThe group of science instruments (Pancam, Mini-TES, APXS, MB, MI, and RAT) is known as the Athena science package. Each rover carried the Athena Science Payload consisting of two remote sensing instruments that viewed the terrain from the top of a mast 154 cm above the ground, four devices for in-situ analysis on the end of a robotic arm and several magnets and calibration targets.\n\n## Individual Instrument Descriptions\n\n**Pancam (Panoramic Camera)**: The Panoramic Camera is known by its nickname, Pancam. Two cameras work in combination to take detailed, multi-wavelength, 3-D panoramic pictures of the Martian landscape surrounding the rover. The rovers' Pancam Mast Assembly stands from the base of the rover wheel 1.4 meters tall (about 5 feet). This height gives the cameras a special \"human geologist´s\" perspective and wide field of view.\n\n**Mini-TES (Miniature Thermal Emission Spectrometer)**: Mini-TES measures the different spectrums of infrared light, or heat, emitted from different minerals in rocks and soils. Mini-TES is specially tuned to look for minerals formed in water.\n\n**APXS (Alpha Particle X-Ray Spectrometer)**: The Alpha Particle X-Ray Spectrometer on the Mars Exploration Rovers, Spirit and Opportunity, is also called the APXS. The APXS reveals the elemental chemistry of rocks and soils by measuring the distinctive way difference materials respond to two kinds of radiation: X-rays and alpha particles.\n\n**Mossbauer Spectrometer (MB)**: This instrument is used for close-up investigations of the mineralogy of iron-bearing samples.\n\n**RAT (Rock Abrasion Tool)**: The Rock Abrasion Tool on the Mars Exploration Rovers, Spirit and Opportunity, is known as the RAT. The RAT's rotating, grinding teeth gnaw into the surface of Martian rock to reveal fresh mineral surfaces for analysis by the rover's scientific tools.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"cb101bab-fec8-4d2c-9813-b97517d86aa9","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:41:27.553Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"551b57e9-6cac-4fb4-a6cd-052b314af5c5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

Its 18-month voyage to Earth's only satellite uncovered a place with the potential to host colossal reservoirs of water ice at its poles, hinted at an iron-rich core, and pinpointed a measly magnetic field.\n\n## Mission End and Crash Impact\n\nThe mission ended on July 31, 1999 at 9:52:02 UT (5:52:02 EDT) when Lunar Prospector was steered into a deliberate collision in a permanently shadowed area of the Shoemaker crater near the lunar south pole. Lunar Prospector hit the crater at 3,800 mph (6,100 km/h), garnering the briefest of flashes that was visible from Earth.\n\n## Scientific Purpose of the Impact\n\nIt was hoped that the impact would liberate water vapor from the suspected ice deposits in the crater and that the plume would be detectable from Earth; however, no such plume was observed.\n\n## Key Discoveries\n\nThe mission successfully detected evidence of water ice before its deliberate crash. In March 1998, NASA announced that data from Lunar Prospector suggested the presence of water ice at both the lunar poles. The neutron spectrometer instrument detected hydrogen, assumed to be in the form of water. The information indicated that a large amount of water ice, possibly about 330 million short tons (300 million metric tons), was mixed into the regolith at each pole, the first direct evidence of water ice at the lunar poles.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"af03232e-21d7-4271-8e2e-3ad386a8b280","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:41:40.045Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"4034127f-e4e6-4a06-8c1c-3c6ff40117c9","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

On orbit, the RPI antennas aboard IMAGE extended 10 m parallel to the spin axis and 250 m in four directions perpendicular to the spin axis, making IMAGE the longest spacecraft then in orbit.\n\n## Dimensions and Specifications\n\nSpecific instrument dimensions (L W H in cm) included: LENA (33 29 31), MENA (38 20 17), HENA (35 38 34), FUV SI (62 36 16), WIC (26 15 13), EUV sensor (15 diameter), and total power requirements of 73.0 kg mass and 54.1 W power.\n\n## Cost\n\nThe total cost of the mission, including spacecraft, launch vehicle and mission operations for the first two years was $154 million.\n\n## Scientific Achievement\n\nIMAGE was designed to observe vast plasma regions of the inner magnetosphere before, during, and after geomagnetic storms using neutral atom imaging (NAI) at various energies, far ultraviolet imaging (FUV), extreme ultraviolet imaging (EUV), and radio plasma imaging (RPI), and these revolutionary instruments provided detailed images of aurora, the ring current, and the plasmasphere at minutes to tens of minute resolution that greatly changed our view of magnetospheric dynamics.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"3583941e-7102-441b-b117-c20604030de9","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:41:53.547Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"f750f659-9c11-41a5-9952-cdf1dfff432e","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

More specifically, all four switches were installed backward, as specified by the Lockheed Martin design, and the parachute never deployed.\n\n## What the Gravity Switches Were Supposed to Do\n\nThe intended design was to make an electrical contact inside the sensor at 3 g (29 m/s²), maintaining it through the maximum expected 30 g (290 m/s²), and breaking the contact again at 3 g to start the parachute release sequence. However, no contact was ever made.\n\n## The Design Flaw Details\n\nThe gravity-switch devices' (or g-switches) installation had been designed incorrectly. The switches flipped, but they were in the wrong position inside the electronic configuration; they could not make the connection needed to start the timing process for parachute deployment.\n\n## The Redundancy Problem\n\nWhile the capsule had redundant switches, this is a redundant system, but because of the design flaw, the exact same flaw is repeated in both systems.\n\n## The Outcome\n\nThe sample return capsule crash-landed in Utah on September 8, 2004, after a design flaw prevented the deployment of its drogue parachute. Despite the crash, scientists were able to recover and analyze the solar wind samples.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"0ad75504-a3b7-46ed-8258-8d3c30b3a4e0","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:42:06.853Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"9b5129a0-b24a-4e75-a7ee-e62f8550e6ff","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

ADS\",\"url\":\"https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2004ApJS..154...10F/abstract\"},{\"title\":\"(PDF) The Infrared Spectrograph (IRS) on the Spitzer Space Telescope\",\"url\":\"https://www.researchgate.net/publication/231086438_The_Infrared_Spectrograph_IRS_on_the_Spitzer_Space_Telescope\"},{\"title\":\"Spitzer Infrared Nearby Galaxies Survey (SINGS) | ISM and Star Formation\",\"url\":\"https://ay201b.wordpress.com/spitzer-infrared-nearby-galaxies-survey/\"}]\n\nBased on the search results, here's comprehensive information about the three main instruments on the Spitzer Space Telescope:\n\n## IRAC (Infrared Array Camera)\n\nIRAC is a four-channel camera that provides simultaneous 5.2 x 5.2 arcmin images at 3.6, 4.5, 5.8, and 8 microns. All four detector arrays in the camera are 256 x 256 pixels in size, with the two short wavelength channels using InSb and the two longer wavelength channels using Si:As IBC detectors.\n\n## IRS (Infrared Spectrograph)\n\nThe Infrared Spectrograph (IRS) provides high- and low-resolution spectroscopy at mid-infrared wavelengths (from 5 to 40 microns). More specifically, the IRS comprises four separate spectrograph modules covering the wavelength range from 5.3 to 38 μm with spectral resolutions, R = λ/Δλ ≈ 90 and 600.\n\n## MIPS (Multiband Imaging Photometer for Spitzer)\n\nMIPS is an imaging camera and spectrometer that detects light in the far-infrared, at wavelengths of 24, 70 and 160 microns. MIPS has three detector arrays in the far infrared (128 × 128 pixels at 24 µm, 32 × 32 pixels at 70 µm, 2 × 20 pixels at 160 µm).\n\nAll three instruments operated during Spitzer's primary cold mission, though IRS and MIPS operated only while the spacecraft was in cold mission mode. The propellers are produced by the gravitational influence of moonlets, lumps of ring material that are estimated to be half a mile (around 1 kilometer) in diameter, which is smaller than a moon but larger than individual ring particles.\n\nThe moonlets launch the surrounding ring particles hundreds of feet above and below the ring, producing the features Cassini imaged. The ring particles are kicked up in the same way that a moving boat creates wake.\n\nIt is estimated that the A Ring contains thousands of such objects. By 2008 over 150 propeller moonlets had been detected.\n\n## Ring Composition and Structure\n\nCassini captured extraordinary ring-moon interactions, observed the lowest ring-temperature ever recorded at Saturn, discovered that the moon Enceladus is the source for Saturn's E ring, and viewed the rings at equinox when sunlight strikes the rings edge-on, revealing never-before-seen ring features and details.\n\nCassini studied features in Saturn's rings called \"spokes,\" which can be longer than the diameter of Earth. Scientists think they're made of tiny icy particles that are lifted by an electrostatic charge and only last a few hours.\n\n## Ring Age\n\nThe findings indicate that Saturn's rings formed between 10 million and 100 million years ago. Cassini's Grand Finale found a relatively low ring mass and clear evidence of ring rain, tipping the scales toward younger rings. Lower mass points to a younger age, because the rings, which are bright and mostly made of ice, would have been contaminated and darkened by interplanetary debris over a longer period.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"c3a056ec-24af-44df-bf0a-6e9235d80415","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:42:58.595Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"064461b1-91c7-4e04-807e-a6ba8bd00d8f","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}

On 15 July 2015, the region was provisionally named \"Tombaugh Regio\" by the New Horizons team in honor of astronomer Clyde Tombaugh, the discoverer of Pluto.\n\n## Sputnik Planitia and Nitrogen Ice Glaciers\n\nPluto's heart is a vast, million-square-mile nitrogen glacier. The center of Sputnik Planum is rich in nitrogen, carbon monoxide, and methane ices. In the northern region of Pluto's Sputnik Planum, swirl-shaped patterns of light and dark suggest that a surface layer of exotic ices has flowed around obstacles and into depressions, much like glaciers on Earth.\n\nEast of Sputnik Planitia are dozens of (mostly) nitrogen-ice glaciers that course down from pitted highlands into the basin, carving out valleys as they go.\n\n## Mountains\n\nWater ice mountains reach 11,000 feet, and the heart's relatively young crater-free surface support the idea that Pluto may have an interior ocean driving the geologic activity.\n\n## Atmosphere and Haze\n\nBacklit by the sun, Pluto's atmosphere rings its silhouette like a luminous halo. The haze extends at least 80 miles above the surface — five times farther than predicted — confirming Pluto's atmosphere. When methane gas in the atmosphere is exposed to ultraviolet light from the sun, it transforms into heavier hydrocarbon gasses that fall to lower, colder parts of Pluto's atmosphere and form ice particles that form a haze, which when exposed to ultraviolet light again, are turned into red organic molecules.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"ea878ef3-57fc-462d-8812-3693ce31c397","timestamp":"2026-03-29T19:43:15.738Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"53f7f16c-f127-47c8-858a-f1027947dc79","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/path/to/projectGSD/dev-tools/gsd-skill-creator","sessionId":"eb657217-f115-4cdc-98b5-170cfdd68c16","version":"2.1.87","gitBranch":"dev","slug":"cheerful-churning-whisper"}
